The erection, excavating, demolition, alteration or repair of any building other than between the hours of 7:00 a.m. and 10:00 p.m. on weekdays is hereby prohibited; except, that the building inspector may determine when the loss or inconvenience that would result to any party in interest is of such a nature as to warrant special consideration, then the building inspector may grant a permit for a period not to exceed ten days for this work to be done between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. 
(7)  Transportation of metal rails, similar materials. The transportation of rails, pillars or columns of iron, steel or other material over and along streets and other public places upon carts, drays, cars, trucks or in any manner so loaded as to cause unreasonably loud noises or as to unreasonably disturb the peace and quiet of those streets or other public places is prohibited. 
(8)  Pile drivers, hammers, similar equipment. The operation between the hours of 10:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m. of any pile driver, steam shovel, pneumatic hammer, derrick, steam or electric hoist or other appliance, the use of which is attended by unreasonably loud or unusual sounds or noises, is prohibited. 
(9)  Blowers and motors. The operation of any noise-creating blower or power fan or any internal combustion engine, the operation of which causes noises due to the explosion of operating gases or fluids, is prohibited unless the noise from this blower or fan is muffled and the engine is equipped with a muffler drive reasonably sufficient to deaden the noise. 
(10)  Sound trucks. The use of mechanical loudspeakers or amplifiers on trucks or other moving or standing vehicles for advertising or other commercial purposes is prohibited. The use of sound trucks for noncommercial purposes during such hours, and with such unreasonable volume as would constitute a public nuisance, is prohibited. 
(11)  Steam whistles. The blowing of any steam whistle attached to any stationary boiler is prohibited; except to give notice of the time to begin or stop work or as a warning of fire or danger upon request of proper authorities. 
(12)  Exhausts. The discharge into the open air of the exhaust of any steam engine, stationary internal combustion engine, motor vehicle, or motorboat is prohibited, except through a muffler or other device which will effectively prevent loud or explosive noises therefrom. 
(13)  Defect in vehicle or load. The use of any automobile, motorcycle or vehicle so out of repair, so loaded or in such manner as to create unreasonably loud and unnecessary grating, grinding, rattling or other noises is prohibited. 
(14)  Loading, unloading, opening boxes. The creation of unreasonably loud and excessive noise in connection with loading or unloading any vehicle or the opening and destruction of bales, boxes, crates and containers is prohibited. 
(15)  Schools, courts, churches, hospitals. The creation of any unreasonably excessive noise on any street adjacent to any school, institution of learning, church or court while the same are in use, or adjacent to any hospital, which unreasonably interferes with the normal operation of the institution, or which disturbs or unduly annoys patients in the hospitals, is prohibited, provided that conspicuous signs are displayed in the streets indicating that it is a school, hospital or court street. 
(16)  Hawkers, peddles, vendors. The shouting and crying of peddlers, hawkers and vendors which disturb the peace and quiet of the neighborhood is prohibited. 
(17)  Noises to attract attention. The use of any drum or other instrument or device for the purpose of attracting attention to any performance, show or sale is prohibited. 
(18)  Operation of motor vehicles. The operation of motor vehicles, including cars, trucks, and motorcycles, upon any parking facility, public or private, vehicle access or pedestrian walkway, or street, public or private, so as to create unreasonable noise and to disturb the peace, quiet and comfort of the inhabitants of the neighborhood. 
(Ord. of 5-11-81; Ord. No. 93-005, 4-12-93) 
Sec. 30-103. - Exceptions. 
The provisions of this article shall not apply to or be enforced against: 
(1)  Any vehicle of the city while engaged in necessary public business. 
(2)  Excavations or repairs of streets by or on behalf of the city, county or state at night when public welfare and convenience renders it impossible to perform this work during the day. 
(3)  The reasonable use of amplifiers or loudspeakers in the course of public addresses which are noncommercial in their character. 
(Ord. of 5-11-81) 
Sec. 30-104. - Violations. 
Any person violating any of the provisions of this article shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-12. 
(Ord. of 5-11-81) 
Secs. 30-105—30-130. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE IV. - NUISANCES[5] 

Footnotes: 
--- (5) --- 
Cross reference— Nuisance animals, § 10-61 et seq. 
State Law reference— Ordinances relating to repair, closing and demolition of dwellings unfit for human habitation, O.C.G.A. § 36-61-11; nuisances, O.C.G.A. § 41-1-1 et seq.; authority to demolish structures where drug crimes are committed, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-7; county or municipal ordinances relating to unfit buildings or structures, O.C.G.A. § 41-2-9; abatement by county of hazard from abandoned well or hole, O.C.G.A. § 44-1-14. 

Sec. 30-131. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Closing means securing and causing a dwelling, building or structure to be vacated. 
Dwellings, buildings, lots or structures means any building or structure or part thereof used or occupied for human habitation, commercial, industrial or business uses, or intended to be so used, and includes any outhouses and appurtenances belonging thereto or usually enjoyed therewith, and also includes any building or structure of any design and all premises wherein such building or structure is located. 
Owner means the holder of the title in fee simple and every security deed holder of record. 
Parties in interest means persons in possession of such property and all individuals, associations and corporations who have interest of record in the county where the property is located in a dwelling, building, lot or structure, including executors, administrators, guardians and trustees. 
(Ord. of 10-12-92, § 1-1) 
Cross reference— Definitions and rules of construction generally, § 1-2. 
Sec. 30-132. - Designation of public officer to exercise statutory nuisance abatement powers. 
The chief of police shall assume all of the duties and exercise such powers as may be necessary or convenient to carry out and effectuate the abatement of nuisances, as set forth in this article, pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 41-2-7—41-2-17. The powers which may be exercised by the chief of police, as the public officer contemplated by this article, in carrying out and effectuating the purpose and provisions of this article, pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 41-2-7—41-2-17, include, without limitation, the following powers in addition to others granted in this article: 
(1)  To investigate the dwelling conditions in the city in order to determine which dwellings, buildings, lots or structures therein are unfit for human habitation or are unfit for current commercial, industrial or business use; 
(2)  To administer oaths and affirmations, to examine witnesses and to receive evidence; 
(3)  To enter upon premises for the purpose of making examinations; provided, however, that such entry shall be made in such manner as to cause the least possible inconvenience to the persons in possession; 
(4)  To appoint and fix the duties of such officers, agents and employees as he deems necessary to carry out the purposes of this article; and 
(5)  To delegate any of his functions and powers under this article to such officers and agents as he may designate. 
(Ord. of 10-12-92, § 1-2) 
Sec. 30-133. - Determination of public officer that dwelling, building, lot or structure is unfit or that a nuisance exists. 
The chief of police, as the public officer contemplated by this article, pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. §§ 41-2-7—41-2-17, may determine, under existing ordinances, that a dwelling, building, lot or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use if he finds that conditions exist in such building, dwelling, lot or structure which are dangerous or injurious to the health, safety or morals of the occupants or such dwelling, building, lot or structure; of the occupants of the neighborhood dwellings, buildings, lots or structures; or of other residences of the city; such conditions may include the following (without limiting the generality of the foregoing): 
(1)  Defects therein increasing the hazards of fire, accidents or other calamities. 
(2)  Lack of adequate ventilation, light or sanitary facilities. 
(3)  Dilapidation. 
(4)  Disrepair. 
(5)  Structural defects. 
(6)  Code violations. 
(7)  Uncleanliness. 
(8)  Presence of substances, or animals or birds, emitting noxious odor or fumes, rubbish, litter, manure, refuse, rubble or trash, overgrown vegetation, malfunctioning private sewage disposal systems, hazaradous objects or any other condition recognized as a nuisance pursuant to state law. 
(9)  The presence of junked motor vehicles or parts thereof in such a condition that they constitute a health hazard or unsightly nuisance as contemplated by O.C.G.A. § 26-60-4. 
(Ord. of 10-12-92, § 1-3; Ord. No. 93-004, 4-12-93) 
Sec. 30-134. - Procedure for abatement of nuisances and other defects. 
(a)  Whenever a request is filed with the public officer by a public authority, to include the fire department, police department, street department, health department or building inspection department, or at least five residents of the city charging that any dwelling, building, lot or structure is unfit for human habitation or for commercial, industrial or business use, or that a nuisance is present, or whenever it appears to the public officer, on his own motion, that any dwelling, building, lot or structure is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use, or that a nuisance is present, the public officer shall, if his preliminary investigation discloses a basis for such charges, issue and cause to be served upon the owner of and any parties in interest in such dwelling, building, lot or structure a complaint stating the charges in that respect and containing a notice that a hearing will be held before the public officer or his designated agent at a place within the county in which the property is located therein, fixed not less than ten days nor more than 30 days after the serving of the complaint; that the owner and any parties in interest shall be given the right to file an answer to the complaint and to appear in person, or otherwise, and give testimony at the place and time fixed in the complaint; and that the rules of evidence prevailing in courts of law or equity shall not be controlling in hearings before the public officer. 
(b)  If, after such notice and hearing, the public officer determines that the dwelling, building, lot or structure under consideration is unfit for human habitation or is unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use, or that a nuisance is present, he shall state in writing his findings of fact in support of such determination and shall issue and cause to be served upon the owner thereof an order: 
(1)  To abate the nuisance. 
(2)  If the repair, alteration or improvement of the dwelling, building, lot or structure can be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, building, lot or structure, requiring the owner or parties in interest, within the time specified in the order, to repair, alter or improve such dwelling, building, lot or structure, so as to render it fit for human habitation or for current commercial, industrial or business use or to vacate and close the dwelling, building, lot or structure as a human habitation; or in the alternative to remove or demolish such dwelling, building, lot or structure. 
(3)  If the repair, alteration or improvement of the dwelling, building, lot or structure cannot be made at a reasonable cost in relation to the value of the dwelling, building, lot or structure, requiring the owner or parties in interest, within the time specified in the order, to remove or demolish such dwelling, building, lot or structure. 
In no event shall the mayor and council of the city require removal or demolition of any dwelling, building, lot or structure except upon a finding that the cost of repair, alteration, or improvement thereof exceeds one-half the value such dwelling, building, lot or structure will have when repaired to satisfy the minimum requirements of this law. The order of the public official shall provide notice to the owner or parties in interest of their right of appeal under O.C.G.A. § 41-2-13. 
(c)  If the owner or parties in interest fail to comply with an order to abate a nuisance or to repair, alter, improve or to vacate and close or demolish the dwelling, building, lot or structure, the public officer may cause such dwelling, building, lot or structure to be repaired, altered or improved or to be vacated and closed or demolished; and the public officer may cause to be posted on the main entrance of any dwelling, building, lot or structure so closed a placard with the following words: 
This building or lot is unfit for human habitation or commercial, industrial or business use; the use or occupation of this building or lot for human habitation or for commercial, industrial or business use is prohibited and unlawful. 
(d)  If the owner fails to comply with any order to abate the nuisance or repair, alter or improve such dwelling, building, lot or structure or remove or demolish the dwelling, building, lot or structure, the public officer may cause the nuisance to be abated or such dwelling, building, lot or structure to be repaired, altered or improved or to be removed or demolished; provided, however, that the duties of the public officer, set forth in subsection (c) of this section and this subsection, shall not be exercised until the city council shall have by ordinance ordered the public officer to proceed to effectuate the purpose of O.C.G.A. §§ 41-2-7—41-2-17 with respect to the particular property or properties which the public officer shall have found to be unfit for human habitation or unfit for its current commercial, industrial or business use, or when a nuisance is present which property or properties shall be described in the ordinance. 
(e)  The amount of the cost of such abating of a nuisance or repair, alteration or improvement or of vacating and closing or removal or demolition by the public officer shall be a lien against the real property upon which such cost was incurred. The lien shall attach to the real property upon the payment of all costs of abating the nuisance or repair or demolition by the city council and the filing of an itemized statement of the total sum of the costs by the public officer in the office of the clerk of court on a lien docket maintained by the clerk for such purposes. If the dwelling, building, lot or structure is removed or demolished by the public officer he shall sell the materials of such dwelling, building, lot or structure and shall credit the proceeds of such sale against the cost of the removal or demolition and any balance remaining shall be deposited in the superior court by the public officer, shall be secured in such manner as may be directed by such court and shall be disbursed by such court to the persons found to be entitled thereto by final order or decree of such court. Nothing in this section shall be construed to impair or limit in any way the power of the city to define and declare nuisances and to cause their removal or abatement by summary proceedings or otherwise. 
(f)  The mayor and council may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for the abatement of the nuisance or repair, alteration or improvement or of removal or demolition of dwellings, buildings, lots or structures only in the following manner: 
(1)  The owner or parties in interest shall be allowed to satisfy the amount due on such lien by paying to the city council within 30 days after the perfection of such lien a sum of money equal to 25 percent of the total amount due and by further paying to city council the remaining balance due on such lien, together with interest at the rate of seven percent per annum, in three equal annual payments, each of which shall become due and payable on the anniversary date of the initial payment made as hereinabove prescribed; 
(2)  Should the property upon which such lien is perfected be sold, transferred or conveyed by the owner or parties in interest at any time prior to the termination of the three-year period, then the entire balance due on such lien shall be due and payable to the city council; and 
(3)  Should the amount due on such lien, or any portion thereof, be unpaid after the passage of the three-year period, or upon the occurrence of the contingency provided for in subsection (2) of this section, the city may enforce the collection of any amount due on such lien for alteration, repair, or removal of structures in the same manner as provided in O.C.G.A. § 48-5-358 and other applicable state statutes. This procedure shall be subject to the right of redemption by any person having any right, title or interest in or lien upon the property, all as provided by O.C.G.A. § 48-4-40 et seq. 
(Ord. of 10-12-92, § 1-4) 
Sec. 30-135. - Service of complaints or orders upon parties in interest and owners of unfit buildings or structures. 
(a)  Complaints or orders issued by the public officer pursuant to the provisions of this article shall, in all cases, be served upon each person in possession of the property, each owner, and each party in interest; and the return of service signed by the public officer or his agent or an affidavit of service executed by any citizen of this state, reciting that a copy of such complaint or orders was served upon each person in possession of the property, each owner, and each party in interest personally, or by leaving such copy at the place of his residence, shall be sufficient evidence as to the service of such person in possession, owner and party in interest. 
(b)  If any of the owners and parties in interest shall reside in the state but outside the city limits of the city, service shall be perfected by causing a copy of such complaint or orders to be served upon such party or parties by the sheriff or any lawful deputy of the county of the residence of such party or parties or such service may be made by any citizen; and the return of such sheriff or lawful deputy or the affidavit of such citizen, that such party or parties were served either personally or by leaving a copy of the complaint or orders at the residence, shall be conclusive as to such service. 
(c)  Nonresidents of this state shall be served by publishing the same once each week for two successive weeks in a newspaper of general circulation within the city limits of the city. A copy of such complaint or orders shall be posted in a conspicuous place on premises affected by the complaint or orders. Where the address of such nonresidents is known, a copy of such complaint or orders shall be mailed to them by registered or certified mail. 
(d)  If either the owner or any party in interest is a minor or an insane person or person laboring under disabilities, the guardian or personal representative resides in the state outside the city limits of the city or is a nonresident, he shall be served as provided for in subsection (b) or (c) of this section. If such minor or insane person or persons laboring under disabilities has no guardian or personal representative or if such minor or insane person lives outside the city limits of the city or is a nonresident, service shall be perfected by serving such minor or insane person personally or by leaving a copy at the place of his residence which shall be sufficient evidence as to the service of such person or persons; in the case of other persons who live outside of the city or are nonresidents, service shall be perfected by serving the judge of the probate court of the county wherein such property is located who shall stand in the place of and protect the rights of such minor or insane person or appoint a guardian ad litem for such person. 
(e)  If the whereabouts of any owner or party in interest is unknown and the same cannot be ascertained by the public officer in the exercise of reasonable diligence and the public officer shall make an affidavit to that effect, then the service of such complaint or order upon such persons shall be made in the same manner as provided in sub 
section (c) of this section or service may be perfected upon any person holding himself out as an agent for the property involved. 
(f)  A copy of such complaint or orders shall also be filed in the proper office or offices for the filing of lis pendens notice in the county in which the dwelling, building or structure is located and such filing of the complaint or orders shall have the same force and effect as other lis pendens notices provided by law. Any such complaint or orders or an appropriate lis pendens notice shall contain a statement to the effect that a lien may arise against the described property and that an itemized statement of such lien is maintained on a lien docket maintained by the city clerk. 
(Ord. of 10-12-92, § 1-5) 
Sec. 30-136. - Injunctions against order to abate a nuisance, repair, close or demolish unfit buildings or structures. 
Any person affected by an order issued by the public officer under this article may petition to the superior court for an injunction pursuant to the provisions of O.C.G.A. § 41-2-13. 
(Ord. of 10-12-92, § 1-6) 
Secs. 30-137—30-160. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE V. - WATERSHED PROTECTION PLAN[6] 

Footnotes: 
--- (6) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 98-7, §§ I—VIII, adopted Mar. 10, 1998, did not specifically amend the Code; hence inclusion as art. V, §§ 30-161—30-168, was at the editor's discretion. 

Sec. 30-161. - Introduction. 
(a)  The Mountain Creek Reservoir (SCS Structure 11) is located in Banks County, Georgia, and owned by Banks County. The reservoir is a soil conservation service rural water supply structure, and water is supplied to Banks County based on storage between specified elevations. The Grove Creek Reservoir is located in Banks County, Georgia and owned by the city. The reservoir is a soil conservation service flood control structure, and water is supplied to the city based on storage between specified elevations. The purpose of this watershed protection plan is to establish criteria pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 12-2-8 for the protection of drinking water watersheds. This protection is necessary for the enhancement of public health, safety and welfare as well as to assure that surface sources of drinking water are of high quality in order to be treated to meet all state and federal drinking water standards. The criteria set forth accomplish this by establishing buffer zones around streams and by specifying allowable impervious surface densities within the identified watersheds. 
(b)  Secondary objectives are to: 
(1)  Manage the reservoir and its drainage area in a manner that will conserve the basic resources of air, soil, and water. 
(2)  Provide for diverse and viable plant, animal, and fish communities. 
(3)  Give special consideration for the protection of threatened and endangered plant and animal species. 
(4)  Manage the reservoir to properly establish, enhance, and maintain acceptable fish and wildlife habitat, aesthetic quality, and sustain natural environmental conditions. 
(5)  Manage use of the reservoir in a manner that provides the least environmental impact. 
(6)  Provide for the protection of public land and water. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § I, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-162. - Definitions. 
For purposes of this watershed protection plan, certain words or terms used herein are defined as follows: 
Buffer means a natural or enhanced vegetated area with no or limited minor land disturbances, such as trails and picnic areas. Buffer setbacks are specified in sections 30-165 and 30-166. 
Corridor means all land within the buffer areas and other setback areas specified in sections 30-165 and 30-166 of this plan. 
Impervious surface means a manmade structure or surface which prevents the infiltration of stormwater into the ground below the structure or surface. Examples are buildings, roads, driveways, parking lots, decks, swimming pools, or patios. No impervious surface areas are allowed within the reservoir buffer area as specified in subsection 30-167(2). 
Land disturbing activity means any grading, scraping, excavating, or filling of land; clearing of vegetation; and any construction, rebuilding, or alteration of a structure. Land disturbing activity shall not include activities such as ordinary maintenance and landscaping operations, individual home gardens, yard and grounds upkeep, repairs, additions or minor modifications to a single-family residence, and the cutting of firewood for personal use. 
Perennial stream means a stream which flows throughout the whole year as indicated on a USGS Quad map. 
Reservoir boundary means the edge of a water supply reservoir defined by its normal pool level. 
Utility means public or private water or sewer piping systems, water or sewer pumping stations, electric power lines, fuel pipelines, telephone lines, roads, driveways, bridges, river/lake access facilities, stormwater systems and railroads or other utilities identified by Banks County, Georgia. 
Water supply reservoir means a governmentally owned impoundment of water for the primary purpose of providing water to one or more governmentally owned public drinking water systems. 
Water supply watershed means the area of land upstream a governmentally owned public drinking water intake. 
Water supply watershed protection plan is a land use plan prepared and adopted by Banks County, Georgia, for the protection of the quality of drinking water obtained from the water supply watershed. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § II, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-163. - Coverage area. 
These criteria shall apply to all governments located within the Grove Creek Watershed and the Mountain Creek Watershed. These criteria do not apply to watersheds not used for public drinking water supply. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § III, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-164. - Exemptions. 
The following activities shall be exempt from the plan: 
(1)  Utilities from the stream corridor buffer and setback area provision of the watershed protection plan in accordance with the following conditions if the utilities to be located in the buffer or setback areas cannot feasibly be located outside these areas: 
a.  The utilities shall be located as far from the stream bank as reasonably possible. 
b.  The installation and maintenance of the utilities shall be such to protect the integrity of the buffer and setback areas as best as reasonably possible. 
c.  The utilities shall not impair the quality of the drinking water stream. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § IV, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-165. - Minimum criteria. 
The Grove Creek Watershed and the Mountain Creek Watershed are classified as a small water supply watershed. Water supply watershed is one that contains less than 100 square miles of land within the drainage basin upstream of a governmentally owned public drinking water supply intake. The Grove Creek Watershed and the Mountain Creek Watershed contains less than 100 square miles of drainage area upstream of the raw water intakes. 
(1)  Stream corridor criteria. 
a.  The perennial stream corridors of a small water supply watershed within a seven-mile radius upstream of a governmentally owned public drinking water supply intake or water supply reservoir are protected by the following criteria: 
1.  A buffer shall be maintained for a distance of 100 feet on both sides of the stream as measured from the stream banks. 
2.  No impervious surface shall be constructed within a 150-foot setback area on both sides of the stream as measured from the stream banks. 
3.  Septic tanks and septic tank drain fields are prohibited in the setback area of subsection a.2. above. 
b.  The perennial stream corridors within a small water supply watershed and outside a seven-mile radius upstream of a governmentally owned public drinking water supply intake or water supply reservoir are protected by the following criteria: 
1.  A buffer shall be maintained for a distance of 50 feet on both sides of the stream as measured from the stream banks. 
2.  No impervious surface shall be constructed within a 75-foot setback area on both sides of the stream as measured from the stream banks. 
3.  Septic tanks and septic tanks drain fields are prohibited in the setback areas of subsection b.2. above. 
c.  The following criteria apply at all locations in a small water supply watershed: 
1.  No sanitary landfills are allowed in the drainage area of the reservoirs. 
2.  New hazardous waste treatment or disposal facilities are prohibited. 
3.  The impervious surface area, including all public and private structures, utilities, or facilities, of the entire water supply watershed shall be limited to 12 percent, or existing use, whichever is greater. Determination of compliance of this subsection c.3. shall be made by the Banks County Zoning Administrator by comparison of proposed development impervious area and existing open space of the reservoir drainage area. The total impervious area ration shall be calculated at time of adoption of this article and maintained in the office of the zoning administrator. 
4.  All permitted and acceptable land disturbing activities will be vegetated or revegetated immediately with appropriate grasses or legumes. 
5.  Harvesting of forest products will be performed in accordance with a harvesting plan agreed to by the Georgia State Forestry Commission and an erosion and sedimentation control plan approved by the soil conservation service. 
6.  Forestry management within the drainage areas will follow the Georgia State Forestry Commission's Best Management Practice Guidelines for Streamside Management Zones, Stream Crossings, Access Roads and Their Construction, Timber Harvesting, Site Preparation, Reforestation and Forest Protection (Prescribed Burning, Firelines, and Chemical Fire Retardant). 
7.  No new commercial livestock operations will be allowed in the drainage areas. Commercial livestock operation is defined as a private or public entity in which livestock are raised for the sole purpose of selling, trading or bartering the livestock or its by-products to the marketplace and the gross revenue of said operations is greater than $5,000.00 per calendar year. Present operations will be allowed to continue only at their present production levels. Agricultural activity shall comply with Georgia Pesticide Act of 1976, Georgia Pesticide and Use Act of 1976, and Georgia Laws 1982, House Bill 1780, (O.C.G.A. § 2-1-4). 
8.  No new land application of animal waste will be allowed without approved nutrient management plan. Such plan will be prepared by either the Soil Conservation Service or the UGA Cooperative Extension Service. 
9.  Broad use of chemical agents such as pesticides are prohibited. Use of pesticides shall be in accordance with Georgia Pesticide Act of 1976, Georgia Pesticide and Use Act of 1976, and Georgia Laws 1982, House Bill 1780, (O.C.G.A.§ 2-1-4). 
10.  Fires or burning on the shoreline are not authorized regardless of the lake level. 
11.  Lot sizes within 1,000 feet of the reservoir pool will be no less than two acres and contain only single-family housing units. 
12.  Commercial and industrial developments shall be restricted to a lot size minimum of five acres within the defined drainage area of the reservoir. 
13.  Permitting for activities in the watershed will be governed by this section, administered by the Banks County Planning Commission. It shall be the responsibility of every land user, developer or builder to present plans for land use alternations within the drainage areas to the Banks County Planning Commission for review and approval. Plans for commercial projects shall bear a stamp by a state registered engineer and shall include at a minimum the calculated total impervious area(s) and shall have a detention/retention pond to control stormwater runoff from the site. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § V, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-166. - Reservoir management plan—Grove Creek Reservoir. 
(a)  Reservoir management. The 307.4-acre Grove Creek Reservoir was constructed in 1978 as a flood relief and control project by the United States Department of Agriculture, Soil Conservation Service (USDA SCS). The city maintains the reservoir. The reservoir shall be governed by a management plan which addresses the recreational use of the reservoir and the maintenance of the buffer around the reservoir. The Grove Creek Reservoir shall be specifically monitored for water quality standards by the city. The reservoir shall be governed by a management plan which addresses the recreational use of the reservoir and the maintenance of the buffer around the reservoir. 
(1)  Recreational uses. The following recreational uses are either prohibited or restricted to protect the water quality of the reservoir for drinking purposes while optimizing its recreational benefits. Public recreation is not a purpose of the Grove Creek Reservoir and such recreation is not encouraged. 
a.  Swimming is prohibited. 
b.  Fishing is allowed. 
c.  Boating will be limited to electric, wind and manual boats only. No floating facilities of any type will be allowed on the reservoir pool. 
d.  Boat docks or similar facilities are prohibited. Existing docks, connecting ramps or boat launch ramps may continue to exist without further improvements or enlargements. 
e.  Public access is not provided other than those existing legal rights-of-way. 
f.  No special events permits will be issued. 
g.  No private shoreline use permits will be issued. 
(2)  Buffer requirements. A buffer shall be maintained for a distance of 150 feet from the normal pool elevation of the reservoir. Should questions concerning the normal pool elevation arise, it shall be resolved by an engineering survey on a case by case basis. The 150-foot buffer shall not be encroached on by any impervious development. Underbrush may be cleared; however, no person shall remove more than 50 percent of the trees eight inches or more in diameter at a point 4.5 feet from natural grade. 
(3)  Reservoir monitoring. The Grove Creek Reservoir is owned fee simple by the city. The city will be responsible for the management of recreational uses and the buffer requirements as defined in the watershed protection plan. The city shall be responsible for the monitoring of the water quality of the watershed. The city shall establish a monitoring plan as follows: 
a.  General inspection of the Grove Creek Watershed once every three years to monitor urban and rural development. 
b.  Aerial inspection of the Grove Creek Watershed once every five years to monitor urban and rural development. 
c.  Establishment of three water quality monitoring points along the perennial streams feeding the reservoir in coordination with GA DNR EPD Water Quality Program. 
d.  Sampling of water samples from the three monitoring points will be coordinated between the city and EPD for report scheduling and parameters with copies of said report filed with the EPD Water Resources Program. 
(b)  Enforcement. Violations of the criteria set forth in this plan for protecting the water quality of the Grove Creek Reservoir shall be enforced by Banks County, assigns or duly authorized agents. All incidents of littering, water pollution, or any other act which threatens water quality, after the first warning, shall be punishable by the maximum fine of $1,000.00 allowed by law in the magistrate court pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et. seq. This is in addition to any other punishment provided by other local, state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 98-6, §§ I, II, 11-23-98; Ord. No. 98-7, § VI, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-167. - Same—Mountain Creek Reservoir. 
The 50.0-acre Mountain Creek Reservoir was constructed in 1993 as a Rural Water Supply project by the United States Department of Agriculture, Soil Conservation Service (USDA SCS). Banks County maintains the reservoir. The reservoir shall be governed by a management plan which addresses the recreational use of the reservoir and the maintenance of the buffer around the reservoir. 
(1)  Recreational uses. The following recreational uses are either prohibited or restricted to protect the water quality of the reservoir for drinking purposes while optimizing its recreational benefits. Public recreation is not a purpose of the reservoir and such recreation is not encouraged. 
a.  Swimming is prohibited. 
b.  Fishing is allowed. 
c.  Boating will be limited to electric, wind and manual boats only. No floating facilities of any type will be allowed on the reservoir pool. 
d.  Boat docks or similar facilities are prohibited. Existing docks, connecting ramps or boat launch ramps may continue to exist without further improvements or enlargements. 
e.  Public access is not provided other than those existing legal rights-of-way. 
f.  No special events permits will be issued. 
g.  No private shoreline use permits will be issued. 
(2)  Buffer requirements. A buffer shall be maintained for a distance of 150 feet from the normal pool elevation (985 feet MSL) of the reservoir. Should questions concerning the normal pool elevation arise, it shall be resolved by an engineering survey on a case by case basis. The 150 foot buffer shall not be disturbed nor shall not be encroached on by any impervious development. 
(3)  Reservoir monitoring. Banks County will be responsible for the management of recreational uses and the buffer requirements as defined in the watershed protection Plan. Banks County shall be responsible for the monitoring of the water quality of the watershed. The city shall establish a monitoring plan as follows: 
a.  General inspection of the Mountain Creek Watershed annually to monitor urban and rural development. 
b.  Aerial inspection of the Mountain Creek Watershed once every three years to monitor urban and rural development. 
c.  Establishment of three water quality monitoring points along the perennial streams feeding the reservoir in coordination with GA-DNR-EPD Water Quality Program. 
d.  Sampling of water samples from the three monitoring points will be coordinated between the County and EPD for report scheduling and parameters with copies of said report filed with the EPD Water Resources Program. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § VII, 3-10-98) 
Sec. 30-168. - Enforcement. 
Violations of the criteria set forth in this plan for protecting the water quality of the Grove Creek and Mountain Creek shall be enforced by Banks County, Georgia, assigns or duly authorized agents. All incidents of littering, water pollution, or infringement of the buffer zone or any other act which threatens water quality, shall be punishable by the maximum fine of $1,000.00 allowed by law in the magistrate court pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et. seq. This is in addition to any other punishment provided by other local, state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 98-7, § VIII, 3-10-98) 
Secs. 30-169—30-180. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VI. - WATER CONSERVATION PLAN[7] 

Footnotes: 
--- (7) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 98-8, §§ I—XI, adopted Nov. 23, 1998, did not specifically amend the Code; hence inclusion as art. VI, §§ 30-181—30-191, was at the editor's discretion. 

Sec. 30-181. - System management. 
Water produced at the water plant from 1991 to 1994 is indicated in Table 1. In Table 2 are records for a 12-month period indicating raw, produced, sold and unaccounted. 
(1)  Unaccounted for water. The city has averaged per month a total of 344,658 gpd of unaccounted for water or 39.2 percent of total water produced from January, 1994, to December, 1994. The city has discovered in April, 1995, a bypass water connection to the Banks County Water System. A meter was in place; however, only a portion of the total amount used was registered. Banks County water use averaged 800,000 to 900,000 gallons per month in 1994. 
Since the discovery and disconnection of the bypass piping, the average daily reading indicated a total of 83,000 gallons was used by Banks County. The monthly average of water produced and water sold by the city in 1994 is 37.225 million gallons and 26.74 million gallons respectively. Using the most recent metered flow to Banks County, less the average monthly billing, the corrected monthly usage by Banks County is 1.7 million gallons. Thus, the average corrected UAW for 1994 is 23.6 percent. 
The filter plant uses an average of 7.5 percent water (as detailed in subsection 30-182(b)). Fire fighting and hydrant flushing account for approximately 1.6 percent of water produced. Therefore, the corrected 1994 UAW average is about 14.5 percent. Please refer to Table 1 and Table 2. 
(2)  UAW elimination programs. 
a.  Leak detection and elimination. The city currently performs leak detection activity by visually checking main water lines. Additional leak detection and elimination measures include the calibration of all meters greater than two inches in size that are three years or older. Random sampling of water meters by selecting one per 25 customers to establish meter types, age of meter and recalibration to determine loss of water. The city also maintains a meter change-out program, whereby old meters are exchanged for recalibrated meters every five to seven years. 
b.  Water distribution system map. The city maintains accurate water distribution maps of the entire system. 
c.  Meter maintenance. The city maintains an active program of testing and calibration of all water meters. Testing procedures shall be as follows: 
TESTING 
1.  All valves shall be tested at the point of manufacture and made driptight when tested under the hydrostatic head specified. After the valves are set in place and are grove to operate, the city shall test them under the rated working pressure and conditions and any valve found to leak shall be made watertight or airtight and if found to be of faulty design shall be satisfactorily repaired or replaced by the city. 
2.  Existing nontouch meters shall be tested in the field as directed by the engineer and/or owner. In addition, existing nontouch meters may be removed and replaced without testing as directed by the engineer and/or owner. Field testing will compare the customer meter to a calibrated meter (a meter that is certified to be accurate) registration. A meter test kit shall include the following: 
(a)  A calibrated meter; 
(b)  Meter yokes; 
(c)  An on-off valve; 
(d)  A flow rate control valve; 
(e)  A meter jumper; 
(f)  Calibration curves; and 
(g)  A supply hose. 
Before testing meter make sure the meter is located where splashing water will not cause any property damage. 
Examine the customer's meter. Make sure that the meter is the correct model and that it is installed in the correct direction. The city will notify customers in writing three days before their service will be interrupted. 
Setting up for the test shall be as follows: 
1.  Turn off the water flow to the meter. 
2.  Remove the customer's meter. 
3.  Attach a hose to the water supply and flush briefly. 
4.  Connect the supply hose to the calibrated meter. 
5.  Install the customer's meter downstream from the test meter to avoid sediment damage to the calibrated meter. 
6.  Connect the drain hose to the customer's meter. 
Performing the field test: 
1.  Turn on the supply, the on-off valve, and open the flow rate valve. Flush briefly to be sure all air is removed form the lines. 
2.  Look for problems with the customer's meter. 
3.  Adjust the flow rate with the flow rate valve to two gpm (gallons per minute). Time it for one minute to get the correct flow. 
4.  Close the on-off valve when the hand on the calibrated meter reaches "o." 
5.  Record the exact reading on the customer's meter. 
6.  Open the on-off valve. Allow ten gallons to run through the calibrated meter, then close the on-off valve immediately. Check the accuracy of the meter. For ten gallons, each mark on the dial equals 1.0 percent accuracy. 
7.  Repeat the test for 15 gpm. Allow 100 gallons to run through the meter. This will take about seven minutes. The hand should make ten complete revolutions. Check the accuracy of the meter. For 100 gallons, each mark on the dial equals 0.1 percent accuracy. 
8.  Repeat the test for one-quarter gpm. Allow ten gallons to run through the meter. This will take about 40 minutes. 
The city shall record all three tests and determine the percent accuracy for each test. This information shall be given to the water superintendent for evaluation and determination of which meters are defective and need replacement. The city shall be sure to identify each meter location by address or other means acceptable to the water superintendent. 
d.  Tank overflow. The 1.5-gallon storage tanks have altitude valves, thereby preventing inadvertent tank overflows. 
e.  Flushing programs. The city will utilize a flushing program for fire hydrants and fire lines. The program shall be accomplished by a comprehensive flushing of the water distribution system, including fire lines on an annual basis. The program may be supplemented by additional flushing as necessary. The flushing program shall encompass the following steps: 
1.  Begin at the supply source working at the first hydrant in the system. Flow water through the streamer nozzle for a duration long enough to empty the pipe section between the source and the hydrant or until the water is clear. 
2.  Proceed to the next hydrant in line. If a branch line extends from the main line between the two hydrants, close the valves to those branch lines until the main line is flushed. Do not close the first hydrant completely until the second hydrant is opened. Flow water through the hydrant as described in step 1. 
3.  Continue the flushing of all lines moving in a direction away form the supply source until all line sections have been flushed. 
f.  Unauthorized use. No person is allowed to use water from any unmetered distribution source. 
g.  Unmetered service connections. There are no unmetered service connections. 
(3)  Interconnections of distribution system. There are three interconnections for the sale of water from the city: One with Banks County, one with Jackson County, and the other to the City of Maysville. A copy of the Agreement is provided in Appendix A1 and A2 [on file in the office of the city clerk]. 
(4)  Additional system management activities. The city maintains a variety of programs designed to aid in the detection of leaks, maintenance and replacement of water meters and water system flushing. It is the desire of the city that each of these programs help to reduce the amount of unaccounted for water loss each month by a goal of ten percent. A ten percent reduction in UAW would result in approximately ten MG per month reduction in produced water. This goal can be achieved by effective monitoring of the water system through: 
a.  Reporting all leaks to the water superintendent immediately and isolating the leak by closing appropriate valves. 
b.  Preventative repairs and upgrades to the system. 
c.  Scheduled meter testing and replacement. 
d.  Scheduled hydrant and line flushing. 
e.  Efficient water plant operation.

Sec. 30-183. - Rate making policies. 
(a)  Listing of all metered and nonmetered connections. 
(1)  There are no nonbilled services in the city. All water services are required to be metered and recorded monthly. The city does not maintain a listing by number of meters for each class of customer. 
(2)  The city has the following service classes as follows: 
a.  Inside water customers includes residential, commercial and industrial users inside city limits. 
b.  Outside water customers includes residential, commercial and industrial users. 
c.  Wholesale customers: 
1.  City of Maysville. 
2.  Banks County. 
(b)  Rate structure. The water and sewer rates are included as appendix B [on file in the office of the city clerk]. 
(c)  Second meters. The city charges a minimum rate for the first 3,000 gallons used and a flat rate per 1,000 gallons or portions thereof over 3,000 gallons. The City of Maysville is charged a flat rate per 1,000 gallons consumed and Banks County is charged based on inside city rates. 
(d)  Price policies. 
(1)  There are no surcharges, discounts or demand charges other than those listed above. 
(2)  The water system is financially self-supporting. 
(3)  The water system is not subsidized by nonwater/sewer revenues. 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § III, 11-23-98) 
Sec. 30-184. - Establishment of water use priorities. 
The city will operate its water system based on a customer use basis. This priority use system shall be in accordance with the city drought contingency plan, section 30-212, is hereby referenced and made part of this water conservation plan. Please see appendix C [on file in the office of the city clerk]. 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § IV, 11-23-98) 
Sec. 30-185. - Plumbing ordinance. 
The city has adopted a water conservation ordinance requiring the use of ultra-low flow plumbing fixtures. This ordinance became effective on June 30, 1991. A copy of said ordinance is attached as appendix D [on file in the office of the city clerk]. 
(1)  Irrigation system. The city does not currently have restrictions on outdoor watering or landscape irrigation systems. 
(2)  Unauthorized use prevention. No person is allowed to use water without prior authorization and proper metering. System usage is monitored daily. 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § V, 11-23-98) 
Sec. 30-186. - Recycle-reuse. 
Recycle-reuse of treated wastewater. There is no current or planned use of recycled of treated wastewater from the city wastewater treatment facility. 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § VI, 11-23-98) 
Sec. 30-187. - Public education. 
(a)  Current education programs. The city has used various programs to increase public awareness for water conservation. The city adopted the Ultra Low Flow Plumbing Ordinance on June 30, 1991. All construction, residential and commercial, since then has been required to utilize ultra-low flow fixtures. 
(b)  Future education programs. The city will publish in the local newspaper, the policies, procedures and the priority use system. Said advertisement shall be published at least once per year. Additionally, four times a year the city will issue printed messages in the billing statement to all customers about water conservation. 
(c)  During droughts or other water shortage emergencies, notices will occur in each publication of the local newspaper, and radio announcements will be made at least once per day. 
(d)  To cultivate a general appreciation for and to encourage the prudent use of water, the city will launch a public education effort by holding public meetings. The purpose is to solicit public input and ideas for water conservation programs. 
(e)  The city manager shall establish a series of public meeting dates within six months of approval of the water conservation plan. Public comments received at the public meetings shall be collected and reviewed by the city manager or his designee. Information received relative to water conservation programs that have been proposed or suggested will be prioritized by the office of the city manager. 
(f)  At the conclusion of the public meetings, all water conservation education programs as proposed, will be presented to the city council for approval. Implementation of the programs shall be on an annual basis at the recommendation of the city manager. The program implementation shall strive to implement three programs within the first three years. A new program shall be added each year thereafter. 
(g)  Several public education programs are being considered such as: 
(1)  Providing retro kits to existing homeowners. These kits would replace older plumbing fixtures with items such as low-flow showerheads, faucet aerators, toilet tank water displacement bags, and other water-conserving devices. For every seven homes successfully retrofitted, the water use of one new home is realized. 
(2)  Newsletter. A quarterly newsletter that will include landscaping tips, guidelines for drought-tolerant gardens, other water conservation issues and the need for conservation. 
(3)  Wastewatchers. A dedicated staff to follow up on customer reports of water waste, leaks, and to respond to consumer questions. 
(4)  Free water surveys. The city will offer free surveys of indoor and outdoor water use to help residential customers increase water use efficiency and lower their water bills. The survey covers faucet flow rates, toilet flushing volumes, irrigation system efficiency and maintenance practices, and how to read the water meter and check for leaks. 
Free water-conserving devices such as low-flow showerheads are offered during the survey. 
(5)  For business and industry. Free surveys of water use and conservation opportunities are offered to commercial and industrial customers in the city service area. Following the survey, customers receive a written report detailing how water is used in their facility and offering conservation recommendations. 
(h)  Additional programs to be implement are provided below: 
(1)  Pamphlets and videos. The city would utilize pamphlets and a water conservation video from the AWWA. These would be made available to the county elementary schools, grades K through 3, for educational training. 
(2)  School program. Provide student activity books and teacher guides on a variety of water supply and conservation topics are provided to county elementary schools. 
(3)  Speakers bureau. Speakers made available to make presentations to schools, community groups and professional organizations. 
(4)  Facility tours. Tours of the water and wastewater facilities to be conducted and their availability are made known to local schools and community groups. 
(5)  For business and industry. Plans for commercial and industrial new construction to be reviewed for conservation opportunities at the time of application for water service. 
Specifically, the following implementation schedule shall be used: 

 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § VII, 11-23-98) 
Sec. 30-188. - Progress report. 
(a)  Twelve-month progress report. The city will submit a progress report 12 months after approval of the water conservation plan by the EPD. The report shall outline actions and/or improvements made to conserve water and reduce water loss in the system. 
(b)  Five-year progress report. The city will submit a progress report five years after approval of the water conservation plan by the EPD. The report shall document water savings achieved by the water system through improvements such as leak detection/repair, meter installation, calibration, or replacement, summer surcharges, and enforcement of ultra-low flow plumbing ordinance. 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § VIII, 11-23-98)

(2)  Average residential GPD per capita. The population for the city in 1990 was 4,108. The Northeast Georgia Regional Development Center has projected the future population growth based on the average annual percentage growth rate which occurred from 1980 to 1988 will continue through the year 2020. Applying an annual growth rate of 1.5 percent, the population of the city will be 6,409 in the year 2020. 
In 1994 the estimated city population was 4,358 as projected by the Northeast Georgia Regional Development Center (NGRDC). Assuming that all residents receive water service from the City, and including those residents served in Jackson County it is estimated that 809,886 gallons per day of water were consumed in 1994 by residents. This equates into approximately 155.1 gallons per day per capita consumed.

Sec. 30-190. - Long range planning. 
Water conservation for long term water demand and supply planning: 
(1)  Per capita projections. In general, per capita water use increases as an area urbanizes. According to the U.S. Geological Survey, this increase is around one gpcd per year in the southeast. However, water conservation efforts such as use of ultra-low flow plumbing fixtures that encourage conservation has recently been implemented. To account for these and future water conservation efforts, it was estimated that the increase in per capita usage would be 0.5 gpcd per year. The increase in per capita use of 0.5 gpcd/year results in a per capita rate of 167.6 gpcd in year 2020. 
(2)  Population projections/population served. From previous reports the population projections for Jackson County and the city are as follows: 

 
In 1995, the total persons served from residential meters is estimated to be: City of Commerce, 4,423; unincorporated Jackson County, 864. This equates to a total of 5,287 persons in 1995. 
In the future, all persons in the City of Commerce and Milner will continue to be served, plus an estimated increase in unincorporated Jackson County. Please refer to Table 5. 
(3)  Water use projections. It is assumed the city's unaccounted for water (UAW) in the future will be by a factor of ten percent (see subsection 30-181(4)). As efforts are made to reduce this rate, additional age of pipes may result in additional leaks. The following notes and assumptions are made to project future water consumed. 
a.  City of Commerce. 
1.  Population to be served as shown in Table 5. 
2.  GPCD to increase 0.5 gpd as discussed in subsection (1) above. 
b.  Banks County. Banks County used an average of 8.8 percent of all water in 1994. This compares to about 10.1 percent of all water sold to inside and outside customers of the city. It is assumed that Banks County will remain using water at the same rate of 10.1 percent of water sold in the city. 
c.  City of Maysville. The City of Maysville water consumption fluctuates throughout the year. In 1994, Maysville consumed approximately 3.5 percent of all water sold. Compared to water sold to inside and outside customers of the city, it is about four percent. It is assumed that the City of Maysville will remain using water at the same rate of four percent of water sold in the city. 
d.  Jackson County. Commerce begin selling water to Jackson County for redistribution and resale by Jackson County in 1995 at a minimum rate of 50,000 gallons per day. It is assumed that this would increase at five percent annually.

Sec. 30-191. - Enforcement. 
Violations of the criteria set forth in this plan shall be enforced by the city, assigns or duly authorized agents. All incidents of littering, water pollution, or any other act which threatens water quality, after the first warning, shall be punishable by the maximum fine of $1,000.00 allowed by law in the magistrate court and/or the city recorder court pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et seq. This is in addition to any other punishment provided by other local, state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 98-8, § XI, 11-23-98) 
Sec. 30-192. - Restriction on outdoor water of landscape. 
(a)  Outdoor watering for purposes of planting, growing, managing, or maintaining ground cover, trees, shrubs, or other plants in the City of Commerce water service area may occur only between the hours of 4:00 p.m. and 10:00 a.m.; provided, however, that this limitation shall not create any limitation upon the following outdoor water uses: 
(1)  Commercial raising, harvesting, or storing of crops; feeding, breeding, or managing livestock or poultry; the commercial production or storing of feed for use in the production of livestock, including, but not limited to, cattle, calves, swine, hogs, goats, sheep, and rabbits, or for use in the production of poultry, including, but not limited to, chickens, hens, ratites, and turkeys; producing plants, trees, fowl, or animals; or the commercial production of aquacultural, horticultural, dairy, livestock, poultry, eggs, and apiarian products or as otherwise defined in O.C.G.A. § 1-3-3; 
(2)  Capture and reuse of cooling system condensate or storm water in compliance with applicable City of Commerce ordinances and state guidelines; 
(3)  Reuse of gray water in compliance with O.C.G.A. § 31-3-5.2 and applicable local board of health regulations; 
(4)  Use of reclaimed wastewater by a designated user from a system permitted by the Environmental Protection Division of the Georgia Department of Natural Resources to provide reclaimed waste water; 
(5)  Watering personal food gardens; 
(6)  Watering new and replanted plant, seed, or turf in landscapes, golf courses, or sports turf fields during installation and for a period of 30 days immediately following the date of installation; 
(7)  Drip irrigation or irrigation using soaker hoses; 
(8)  Hand watering with a hose with automatic cutoff or handheld container; 
(9)  Use of water withdrawn from private water wells or surface water by an owner or operator of property is such well or surface water is on said property; 
(10)  Watering horticultural crops held for sale, resale, or installation; 
(11)  Watering athletic fields, golf courses, or public turf grass recreational areas; 
(12)  Installation, maintenance, or calibration of irrigation systems; or 
(13)  Hydroseeding. 
(b)  No person shall use or allow the use of water in violation of the restrictions on outdoor water use contained in this section. Violations of this section shall be punishable in accordance with section 1-12 of this Code. 
(Ord. No. 2010-016, 12-13-10) 
Secs. 30-193—30-210. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VII. - DROUGHT CONTINGENCY PLAN[8] 

Footnotes: 
--- (8) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 98-9, §§ I—IV, adopted Nov. 23, 1998, did not specifically amend the Code; hence inclusion as art. VII, §§ 30-211—30-214, was at the editor's discretion. 

Sec. 30-211. - Drought conditions. 
(a)  Drought indicators. 
(1)  Streamflow levels. Streamflow levels do not apply in this project. 
(2)  Groundwater levels. Groundwater levels do not apply in this project. 
(3)  Reservoir storage or levels. Reservoir water surface levels will be monitoried to determine storage available for water supply, using a U.S.G.S. staff gauge or equivalent. A drought will defined as any decrease in available water supply such that the Grove Creek Reservoir's pool elevation is less than elevation 695.6 for 72 hours or more, based on a 4.2 MGD average daily withdrawal rate. This elevation is equal to the low water surface level for 1954 drought conditions under a 4.2 MGD average daily withdrawal rate. It is estimated that a pool level of 695.6 the reservoir water suupply allocation can only supply 30 additional days of water at a 4.2 MGD rate is drought conditions persist. 
The city will phase drought restrictions based on a certain level drop in the reservoir pool elevation. At such time as the reservoir pool elevation drops one foot from elevation 697.6 (normal pool) to 696.6. for 72 hours, the city will implement Level One drought restrictions. When the pool elevation drops to 695.6 for 72 hours, the city will enact Level Two drought restrictions. 
(4)  Drought restriction levels. 
a.  Level One: Outdoor water use may occur only on scheduled days within the hours of 12:00 midnight to 10:00 a.m. The scheduled days for odd numbered addresses are Tuesdays, Thursdays and Sundays. The scheduled days for even numbered addresses and golf course fairways are Mondays, Wednesdays and Saturdays. The following uses are prohibited: 
1.  Using hydrants for any purpose other than fire fighting, public health, safety or flushing. 
2.  Washing hard surfaces such as streets, gutters, sidewalks and driveways, except when necessary for public health and safety. 
b.  Level Two: No outdoor water use is allowed other than for retail garden centers, producers of food and fiber and commercial car washes. 
Violations of drought restriction levels shall be punished as provided in section 30-212. 
(Ord. No. 98-9, § I, 11-23-98; Ord. No. 2007-11, 11-12-07) 
Sec. 30-212. - Priority use system. 
(a)  Order of water use. The city will operate its water system based on a customer priority use basis. This priority system is developed to ensure adequate water supply to users in order of need as follows: 
(1)  Hospitals, nursing homes and other convalescent care facilities. 
(2)  Domestic personal uses including personal consumption, bathing, dish and clothes washing. 
(3)  Industrial uses. 
(4)  Commercial uses. 
(5)  Schools. 
(6)  Farm uses for acreage greater than ten acres including plant nurseries. 
(7)  Noncommercial uses including farms and plant nurseries not exceeding ten acres and outdoor domestic watering. 
(8)  Outdoor recreation. 
(b)  When in effect. The priority use system shall be placed in effect when either the normal pool drops from elevation 697.6 to 695.6 or when there is computed less than 75 percent available water remaining to meet the average annual daily withdrawal of the preceding 12 months. 
(c)  When used during water shortages. The city shall adopt the priority use system as outlined in II-A for use during periods of water shortages. Water shortages may be declared for reasons other than lack of supply. 
(d)  Restrictions and enforcement. During periods of drought (when the reservoir pool elevation in 695.6 or less) or other emergency water reduction restrictions on water use shall apply to the following priority uses: 
(1)  Industrial uses in which water is required for production of products shall be reduced by 50 percent of the average daily amount as computed by the past 12 months of usage. 
(2)  Commercial uses shall be restricted to cooking and sanitary needs only. Commercial car washes will be prohibited while priority use system is in effect. 
(3)  Noncommercial uses such as outdoor watering shall be prohibited. 
(4)  Outdoor water recreation activities shall be prohibited. 
Enforcement procedures shall call for all city employees to report any observed, reported or suspected infraction to the city manager. The first violation shall be a verbal warning to cease restricted water use. Additional violations shall be accessed as follows: 
Second violation—$100.00 surcharge; 
Third violation—$200.00 surcharge; 
Subsequent violations—$200.00 surcharge and lock meter box plus a $300.00 reconnection fee. 
(e)  Emergency procedures and rationing. The city manager shall be notified by the director of water and sewer operation in the event that the normal pool elevation drops to elevation 696.6. The city manager shall then obtain authorization from the city council to implement Level One drought restrictions. The city manager shall be notified by the director of water and sewer operations in the event that the normal pool elevation drops to elevation 695.6. The city manager shall then obtain autorization from the city council to implement Level Two drought restrictions and to put the priority use system into effect. In the event Level One or Level Two drought restrictions are implemented, the city manager shall also contact Banks County, Jackson County, the Jackson County Water and Sewer Authority and the City of Maysville. The following procedures shall aso be followed: 
(1)  Announcement over local radio, advertisement by local legal newspaper and printed messages sent with monthly water billings concerning drought restrictions. 
(2)  Area schools, hospitals and largest water customers shall be notified in writing. 
(3)  In the event of severe water shortage, such that rationing measures are required, steps (1) and (2) above shall be followed as outlined. 
(4)  Rationing or water supplies shall be directed by the city manager's office. Water for uses other than items described in subsection (a)(1) and (2) shall be prohibited. 
(Ord. No. 98-9, § II, 11-23-98; Ord. No. 2007-11, 11-12-07) 
Sec. 30-213. - State mandated restrictions. 
The city shall also implement and enforce any state mandated restrictions which are more restrictive than city mandated water restrictions in effect at the time that such state mandated water restrictions are declared. 
(Ord. No. 98-9, § III, 11-23-98; Ord. No. 2007-11, 11-12-07) 
Sec. 30-214. - Enforcement. 
Violations of the criteria set forth in this plan for protecting the water quality of the Grove Creek Reservoir shall be enforced by the city, assigns or duly authorized agents. All incidents of littering, water pollution, or any other act which threatens water quality, after the first warning, shall be punishable by the maximum fine of $1,000.00 allowed by law in the magistrate court pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 15-10-60 et seq. This is in addition to any other punishment provided by other local, state or federal law. 
(Ord. No. 98-9, § IV, 11-23-98) 
Secs. 30-215—20-230. - Reserved. 
ARTICLE VIII. - STREAM BUFFER PROTECTION 

Sec. 30-231. - Title. 
This article shall be known as the "City of Commerce Stream Buffer Protection Ordinance." 
(Ord. No. 2004-028A, § 1, 12-13-2004) 
Sec. 30-232. - Findings and purposes. 
(a)  Findings. Whereas, the city finds that buffers adjacent to streams provide numerous benefits including: 
(1)  Protecting, restoring and maintaining the chemical, physical and biological integrity of streams and their water resources. 
(2)  Removing pollutants delivered in urban stormwater. 
(3)  Reducing erosion and controlling sedimentation. 
(4)  Protecting and stabilizing stream banks. 
(5)  Providing for infiltration of stormwater runoff. 
(6)  Maintaining base flow of streams. 
(7)  Contributing organic matter that is a source of food and energy for the aquatic ecosystem. 
(8)  Providing tree canopy to shade streams and promote desirable aquatic habitat. 
(9)  Providing riparian wildlife habitat. 
(10)  Furnishing scenic value and recreational opportunity. 
(11)  Providing opportunities for the protection and restoration of greenspace. 
(b)  Purposes. It is the purpose of this article is to protect the public health, safety, environment and general welfare; to minimize public and private losses due to erosion, siltation and water pollution; and to maintain stream water quality by provisions designed to: 
(1)  Create buffer zones along the streams of the city for the protection of water resources; and, 
(2)  Minimize land development within such buffers by establishing buffer zone requirements and by requiring authorization for any such activities. 
(Ord. No. 2004-028A, § 2, 12-13-04) 
Sec. 30-233. - Definitions. 
Buffer means, with respect to a stream, a natural or enhanced vegetated area (established by subsection 30-235(a) below), lying adjacent to the stream. 
Impervious cover means any manmade paved, hardened or structural surface regardless of material. Impervious cover includes but is not limited to rooftops, buildings, streets, roads, decks, swimming pools and any concrete or asphalt. 
Land development means any land change, including but not limited to clearing, grubbing, stripping, removal of vegetation, dredging, grading, excavating, transporting and filling of land, construction, paving and any other installation of impervious cover. 
Land development activity means those actions or activities which comprise, facilitate or result in land development. 
Land disturbance means any land or vegetation change, including, but not limited to, clearing, grubbing, stripping, removal of vegetation, dredging, grading, excavating, transporting and filling of land, that do not involve construction, paving or any other installation of impervious cover. 
Land disturbance activity means those actions or activities which comprise, facilitate or result in land disturbance. 
Floodplain means any land area susceptible to flooding, which would have at least a one percent probability of flooding occurrence in any calendar year based on the basin being fully developed as shown on the current land use plan; i.e., the regulatory flood. 
Parcel means any plot, lot or acreage shown as a unit on the latest county tax assessment records. 
Permit means the permit issued by the Natural Resource Conservation Service (NRCS) required for undertaking any land development activity 
Person means any individual, partnership, firm, association, joint venture, public or private corporation, trust, estate, commission, board, public or private institution, utility, cooperative, city, county or other political subdivision of the state, any interstate body or any other legal entity. 
Protection area, or stream protection area means, with respect to a stream, the combined areas of all required buffers and setbacks applicable to such stream. 
Riparian means belonging or related to the bank of a river, stream, lake, pond or impoundment. 
Setback means, with respect to a stream, the area established by subsection 30-235(a)(2) extending beyond any buffer applicable to the stream. 
Stream means any stream, beginning at: 
(1)  The location of a spring, seep, or groundwater outflow that sustains streamflow; or 
(2)  A point in the stream channel with a drainage area of 25 acres or more; or 
(3)  Where evidence indicates the presence of a stream in a drainage area of other than 25 acres, the city may require field studies to verify the existence of a stream. 
Stream bank means the sloping land that contains the stream channel and the normal flows of the stream. 
Stream channel means the portion of a watercourse that contains the base flow of the stream. 
Watershed means the land area that drains into a particular stream. 
(Ord. No. 2004-028A, § 3, 12-13-04) 
Sec. 30-234. - Applicability. 
This article shall apply to all land development activity on property containing a stream protection area as defined in section 30-233. These requirements are in addition to, and do not replace or supersede, any other applicable buffer requirements established under state law and approval or exemption from these requirements do not constitute approval or exemption from buffer requirements established under state law or from other applicable local, state or federal regulations. 
(1)  Grandfather provisions. This article shall not apply to the following activities: 
a.  Work consisting of the repair or maintenance of any lawful use of land that is zoned and approved for such use on or before the effective date of this article. 
b.  Existing development and on-going land disturbance activities including but not limited to existing agriculture, silviculture, landscaping, gardening and lawn maintenance, except that new development or land disturbance activities on such properties will be subject to all applicable buffer requirements. 
c.  Any land development activity that is under construction, fully approved for development, scheduled for permit approval or has been submitted for approval as of the effective date of this article. 
d.  Land development activity that has not been submitted for approval, but that is part of a larger master development plan, such as for an office park or other phased development that has been previously approved within two years of the effective date of this article. 
(2)  Exemptions. The following specific activities are exempt from this article. Exemption of these activities does not constitute an exemption for any other activity proposed on a property. 
a.  Activities for the purpose of building one of the following: 
• A stream crossing by a driveway, transportation route or utility line; 
• Public water supply intake or public wastewater outfall structures; 
• Intrusions necessary to provide access to a property; 
• Public access facilities that must be on the water including boat ramps, docks, foot trails leading directly to the river, fishing platforms and overlooks; 
• Unpaved foot trails and paths; 
• Activities to restore and enhance stream bank stability, vegetation, water quality and/or aquatic habitat, so long as native vegetation and bioengineering techniques are used. 
b.  Public sewer line easements paralleling the creek, except that all easements (permanent and construction) and land disturbance should be at least 25 feet from the top of the bank. This includes such impervious cover as is necessary for the operation and maintenance of the utility, including but not limited to manholes, vents and valve structures. This exemption shall not be construed as allowing the construction of roads, bike paths or other transportation routes in such easements, regardless of paving material, except for access for the uses specifically cited in subsection a., above. 
c.  Land development activities within a right-of-way existing at the time this article takes effect or approved under the terms of this article. 
d.  Within an easement of any utility existing at the time this article takes effect or approved under the terms of this article, land disturbance activities and such impervious cover as is necessary for the operation and maintenance of the utility, including but not limited to manholes, vents and valve structures. 
e.  Emergency work necessary to preserve life or property. However, when emergency work is performed under this section, the person performing it shall report such work to the chief building official on the next business day after commencement of the work. Within ten days thereafter, the person shall apply for a permit and perform such work within such time period as may be determined by the chief building official to be reasonably necessary to correct any impairment such emergency work may have caused to the water conveyance capacity, stability or water quality of the protection area. 
f.  Forestry and silviculture activities on land that is zoned for forestry, silvicultural or agricultural uses and are not incidental to other land development activity. If such activity results in land disturbance in the buffer that would otherwise be prohibited, then no other land disturbing activity other than normal forest management practices will be allowed on the entire property for three years after the end of the activities that intruded on the buffer. 
After the effective date of this article, it shall apply to new subdividing and platting activities. 
Any land development activity within a buffer established hereunder or any impervious cover within a setback established hereunder is prohibited unless a variance is granted pursuant to subsection 30-235(b). 
(Ord. No. 2004-028A, § 4, 12-13-04) 
Sec. 30-235. - Land development requirements. 
(a)  Buffer and setback requirements. All land development activity subject to this article shall meet the following requirements: 
(1)  An undisturbed natural vegetative buffer shall be maintained for 50 feet, measured horizontally, on both banks (as applicable) of the stream as measured from the top of the stream bank. 
(2)  An additional setback shall be maintained for 25 feet, measured horizontally, beyond the undisturbed natural vegetative buffer, in which all impervious cover shall be prohibited. Grading, filling and earthmoving shall be minimized within the setback. 
(3)  No septic tanks or septic tank drain fields shall be permitted within the buffer or the setback. 
(b)  Variance procedures. Variances from the above buffer and setback requirements may be granted in accordance with the following provisions:
