When a telecommunications facility will be a use as of right pursuant to section 78-124 and requires only a building permit and design review before it may be erected, the director will expedite review of the application and render a decision on the application within five business days after receipt of a complete application. 
(c)  Special use permits. 
(1)  A request for a special use permit shall be initiated by application to the director and handled in accordance with the special use permit provision of section 10.7 of the zoning ordinance. The mayor and city council may issue a special use permit under this section provided it shall have determined that all of the requirements of section 78-126 have been satisfied and, further, that the benefits of and need for the proposed tower are greater than any possible depreciating effects and damage to the neighboring properties. 
(2)  In granting a special use permit, the mayor and city council may impose additional zoning conditions to the extent determined necessary to buffer or otherwise minimize adverse effects of the proposed tower or antenna on surrounding properties. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-128. - Co-location. 
Applicant and owner shall allow other future personal wireless service companies, including public and quasi-public agencies, using functionally equivalent personal wireless technology to co-locate antennae, equipment and facilities on a telecommunications facility unless specific technical constraints prohibit said co-location. Applicant and other personal wireless carriers shall provide a mechanism for the construction and maintenance of shared facilities and infrastructure and shall provide for equitable sharing of cost in accordance with industry standards. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-129. - Appeals. 
Appeals from any decision of the director may be taken by any person aggrieved or any official of the city affected by the decision of the director. Such appeal shall be to the board of zoning appeals pursuant to article XII of the zoning ordinance. Appeals from any decision of the board of zoning appeals shall be made to the superior court within 30 days of the decision by a writ of certiorari. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-130. - Nuisances. 
Telecommunications facilities, including, without limitation, power source, ventilation and cooling, shall be operated at all times within the limits of the city noise ordinance, shall not be operated so as to cause the generation of heat that adversely affects a building occupant and shall not be maintained or operated in such a manner as to be a nuisance. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-131. - Removal of antennae and towers. 
All telecommunications facilities shall be maintained in compliance with standards contained in applicable building and technical codes so as to ensure the structural integrity of such facilities. If upon inspection by the director any such telecommunications facility is determined not to comply with the code standards or to constitute a danger to persons or property, then upon notice being provided to the owner of the facility and the owner of the property if such owner is different, such owners shall have 30 days to bring such facility into compliance. In the event such telecommunications facility is not brought into compliance within 30 days, the city may provide notice to the owners requiring the telecommunications facility to be removed. In the event such telecommunications facility is not removed within 30 days of receipt of such notice, the city may remove such facility and place a lien upon the property for the costs of removal. Delay by the city in taking action shall not in any way waive the city's right to take action. The city may pursue all legal remedies available to it to insure that telecommunications facilities not in compliance with the code standards or which constitute a danger to persons or property are brought into compliance or removed. The city may seek to have the telecommunications facility removed regardless of the owner's or operator's intent to operate the tower or antenna and regardless of any permits, federal, state or otherwise, which may have been granted. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-132. - Abandoned towers. 
(a)  Any telecommunications facility that is not operated for a continuous period of 12 months shall be considered abandoned, whether or not the owner or operator intends to make use of it or any part of it. The owner of a telecommunications facility and the owner of the property where the facility is located shall be under a duty to remove the abandoned telecommunications facility. If such antenna and/or tower is not removed within 60 days of receipt of notice from the city notifying the owner(s) of such abandonment, the city may remove such tower and/or antenna and place a lien upon the property for the costs of removal. The city may pursue all legal remedies available to it to insure that abandoned telecommunications facilities are removed. Delay by the city in taking action shall not in any way waive the city's right to take action. The city may have the telecommunications facility removed regardless of the owner's or operator's intent to operate the tower or antenna and regardless of any permits, federal, state or otherwise, which may have been granted. 
(b)  If the owner of an abandoned tower or antenna wishes to use such abandoned tower or antenna, the owner first must apply for and receive all applicable permits and meet all of the conditions of this article as if such tower or antenna were a new tower or antenna. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-133. - Pre-existing towers/nonconforming uses. 
(a)  All telecommunications facilities operative on November 8, 1999, shall be allowed to continue their present usage as a nonconforming use and shall be treated as a nonconforming use in accordance with section 6.1 of the zoning ordinance. Routine maintenance, including replacement with a new tower or antenna of like construction and height, shall be permitted on such existing telecommunications facilities. New construction other than routine maintenance shall comply with the requirements of this article. 
(b)  A telecommunications facility that has received city approval as of November 8, 1999, in the form of either a building permit or special use exception, but has not yet been constructed or placed in operation shall be considered an existing telecommunications facility so long as such approval is current and not expired. 
(c)  Placement of an antenna on a nonconforming structure shall not be considered an expansion of the nonconforming structure. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-134. - Penalty for violation of article. 
(a)  Any person who attempts to erect or erects a telecommunications facility covered by this article without having first obtained the necessary building permit, special use permit or variance in the manner provided in this article shall be deemed in violation of this article. Any responsible party or other persons convicted by a court of competent jurisdiction of violating any provision of this article shall be guilty of violating a duly adopted ordinance of the city and shall be punished either by a fine not to exceed $1,000.00 or by imprisonment not to exceed 180 days or both. The court shall have the power and authority to place any person guilty of violation of this article on probation and to suspend or modify any fine or sentence. As a condition of such suspension, the court may require payment of restitution or impose other punishment allowed by law. 
(b)  If any structure is erected, constructed, reconstructed, altered, repaired, converted or maintained in violation of this article or without obtaining that required permits, or if any building, structure or land is used in violation of this article, the city attorney, in addition to any other remedies, may institute proceedings to prevent such unlawful erection, construction, reconstruction, alteration, conversion, maintenance or use or to correct or abate such violations. Each and every day such unlawful erection, construction, reconstruction, alteration, conversion, maintenance or use continues may be deemed a separate offense. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Sec. 78-135. - Coordination with federal law. 
Whenever the governing authority finds that the application of this article would unreasonably discriminate among providers of functionally equivalent personal wireless services or prohibit or have the effect of prohibiting the provision of personal wireless services, a conditional use permit waiving any or all of the provisions of this article may be granted. 
(Ord. No. 99-09, § 1, 11-8-99) 
Chapter 82 - TAXICABS[1] 

Footnotes: 
--- (1) --- 
Editor's note— Ord. No. 2017-0900, adopted November 20, 2017, repealed ch. 82 and enacted a new ch. 82 as set out herein. Former ch. 82 pertained to vehicles for hire and derived from Ord. No. 93-008, adopted April 12, 1993. 

Sec. 82-1. - Definitions. 
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this article, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly indicates a different meaning: 
Open stand means locations on the streets of the city that may be used by any taxicab on a nonexclusive, first-come-first-served basis, and not by private vehicles or other public conveyances. 
Taxicab means a motor vehicle used to transport passengers for a fee or fare and which is fitted with a taximeter or other device that is used to compute such fee or fare. Taxicabs shall not include limousine carriers or ride share drivers as defined in O.C.G.A. §40-1-90(1) and (3). 
Taxicab company means an entity or person operating a taxicab or providing taxi services as defined in O.C.G.A. § 40-1-90(5). 
Taximeter means an instrument or device attached to a motor vehicle and designed to measure the distance traveled by such vehicle, or an instrument or device attached to a motor vehicle and designed to compute and indicate the fare or fee to be charged to the passenger. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-2. - Doing business defined. 
Any taxicab company operating a taxicab within the incorporated boundaries of the city or with an established business relationship with independent contractors operating a taxicab shall be deemed doing business in the city under this article if such person is picking up passengers in the city and accepting or soliciting any consideration, charge or fee which is determined by agreement, by mileage, by the length of time the vehicle is used or by contract for the use of any motor vehicle or other vehicle designed or used for the purpose of transporting passengers. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-3. - Compliance. 
No person or entity shall do business as a taxicab company in the city without first meeting the requirements of state law and obtaining a taxicab company business license. No person or entity shall operate a taxicab without a for-hire license endorsement or a private background check pursuant to O.C.G.A. § 40-5-39. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-4. - Taxicab company permit holder's responsibilities for violations. 
Taxicab company business license's holder(s) are responsible for violations of this article by their employees and independent contractors, including company drivers and dispatchers. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-5. - Taxicab company permits generally. 
(a)  An applicant for a taxicab company business license is required to provide information showing its qualifications on a form provided by the city clerk. 
(b)  No taxicab company business shall be issued to an applicant unless the applicant has a valid and current license to do business in the state and all other licenses required by the state, 
(c)  The business license required by the provisions of this article shall expire on December 31 of each year. 
(d)  All applicants must: 
(1)  Provide a verifiable dispatch location staffed by company agents or employees, have a published telephone number and have sufficient parking to accommodate its taxicabs when not in use; 
(2)  Comply with requirements of state law for transportation referral service providers, as defined in O.C.G.A. § 40-1-190(8); 
(3)  Provide a copy of the applicant's rate schedule and the daily hours of operation; and 
(4)  Provide the name, address and telephone number of a responsible individual residing in the county who will be the registered agent for the purpose of service of process or receipt of citations. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-6. - Insurance. 
All companies licensed pursuant to the provisions of this article shall maintain for the duration of their business license minimum insurance coverage as required by state law for vehicles and drivers. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-7. - Transfer and term of permits. 
No taxicab company business license is transferable; and they shall expire annually as provided in this article. If not renewed in compliance with this article, all such licenses shall expire annually and be of no further force and effect. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-8. - Certificate. 
The city manager may periodically require the owner or operator of a taxicab to submit a copy of the State of Georgia certificate of inspection for the information of the police department and the mayor and council. The certificate shall be in the form prescribed by Georgia law. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-9. - Suspension, revocation—Grounds. 
The willful violation of any ordinance of the city or the laws of the state shall be grounds for the suspension or permanent revocation of a taxicab business license as set out in this division. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-10. - Same—Power of city manager. 
When the mayor and council are not in session, the city manager shall have the authority and power, in his discretion, upon sufficient evidence or information, to suspend the business license of any taxicab owner or operator for a period of 30 days by a written order, a copy of which shall be served upon the owner or operator of a taxicab within two days after the suspension of his license, and he shall address a communication in writing to the council of his action in suspending such permit and the reason therefor. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-11. - Same—Appeal. 
The owner or operator of a taxicab shall be entitled to a hearing before the mayor and council upon application therefor, for the body to determine whether or not the suspension of his license to operate a taxicab shall be made permanent or not within the city; provided such application is filed with the city clerk within five days from the date of suspension by the city manager. If no appeal is filed then the suspension may be stopped, continued or made permanent by the council at its next regular meeting, 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-12. - Operation of taxicab during suspension. 
It shall be unlawful for an owner or operator or any driver employed by such owner or operator during the period of suspension of a taxicab business license to furnish service and a violation of this section shall, upon conviction, be punished as provided in section 1-12. Such penalty shall be in addition to the suspension. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-13. - Disposition of business license during suspension. 
Any taxicab license of any owner or operator in the city which has been suspended shall be returned to the city manager, to be retained by him during the period of suspension or until the suspension is revoked and relieved by the mayor and council. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-14. - Revocation. 
If the suspension of a taxicab license is made permanent and the license is revoked by the mayor and council, the license shall be canceled by the city manager. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-15. - Taxicab zones. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to park or cause to be parked any vehicle except a taxicab within those areas where the curbing is marked by lines and where there is a sign denoting the same as a parking space for taxicabs only, such areas being reserved for the use of taxicabs only. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-16. - Driver's license. 
No taxi driver shall operate a taxicab in the city before the person who is to drive the taxicab is approved for driving a motor vehicle by the state department of public safety. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-17. - Owner's identification, rate card displayed. 
(a)  Every taxicab shall display inside the cab, at a convenient place visible to passengers, a card not less than two inches in width by four inches in length, which shall have printed thereon the name, business address and telephone number of the owner and the rates charged for the use of such vehicle. 
(b)  Every such car shall have displayed on each side thereof the name and telephone number of the owner in letters and numerals of such size as to be readily visible to the public, and not less than three inches high. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17) 
Sec. 82-18. - Fare—Refusal to pay. 
It shall be unlawful for any person to use a motor vehicle operated as a taxicab and refuse to pay therefor. 
(Ord. No. 2017-0900, 11-20-17)
